  Hello Lafkon friends,

  My name is Laura Fernández. I am writing to you on behalf of
  Medialab-Prado <http://medialab-prado.es> to invite you to work with us
  in the design of acampaign for the upcoming international Libre Graphics
  Meeting <http://libregraphicsmeeting.org/> which will take place at
  Medialab-Prado (Madrid) in April 2013, together with a two-week workshop
  for collaborative prototyping of projects under the topic:"Tools for a
  read-write world" <http://medialab-prado.es/article/ilgru_call_projects>.

  We would very much like to work with you because we are aware of the
  work you have done for events such as makeart 2010
  http://makeart.goto10.org/2010 , which we really appreciate and find in
  line with the kind of process and result we would like to have.

  I send below an outline of the work we would be asking for, hoping you
  will find it interesting!

  I wait for your answer, please contact me also for any question you
  might have. I am cc'ing Hajo Doorn (Worm <http://www.worm.org/>,
  Rotterdam) and Femke Snelting (Constant
  <http://www.constantvzw.org/site/>, Brussels) who are also part of the
  organising group for the event-campaign.

  Best regards,

  Laura Fernández


  +++++++++++++

  The design/campaign compliments existing identities (LGM, Medialab
  Prado, various partners) and does not need to replace them.

  *What do we want to achieve?*
  -Make publicity of the event in April in a way that at the same time
  involves in the process the different voices of people and communities
  we would like to reach
  -Reflects in the campaign questions and prejudices around the topic

  *What are we asking for?*
  -Design and programming of an online generative tool to create the
  graphic materials for the campaign in a way that includes audience's
  voice (text, images)
  -Online space where this can happen, ideally for mobile devices too
  -Design/selection of final "official" poster
  -Logoor image that can be included in various media
  -Everything needs to bedeveloped with FLOSS-tools/technologies.
  Scriptsand results can be freely worked with.(GPL license or similar)
  *Dates:*
  -16th December first draft-ideas (at some point Hajo Doorn would travel
  to your studio to discuss)
  -15th January the generative script is online
  -15th March "official" poster
  -10-13 April: event
  **
  *Fees for design and development*: 4.000EURincl. TVA

  Production will happen in Madrid

  *Some references:*
  -Brainstorming last week's meeting:http://future.hotglue.me/edit
  <http://future.hotglue.me/edit>
  user: future // pword: FutureTools
  -Visual identity of LGM in past events: http://libregraphicsmeeting.org
  -Old typography taken from Medialab-Prado's building, recently
  digitalised at this workshop:
  http://manufacturaindependente.com/piedranave/  See fonts:
  http://manufacturaindependente.com/piedranave/letras/
  -DIY slogans and banners at 15 May demonstrations in Spain:
  http://sociologiac.net/2012/05/07/manuel-castells-estamos-cambiando-el-mundo-disculpen-las-molestias/


  Other:
  -Easy to use more languages(Spanish and English)
  -Filter content? How?
  -We will need to include EU and City Council's Madrid logos at least in
  some contexts and in final poster

  --
  Laura Fernández
  Medialab Prado
  Área de Las Artes, Ayuntamiento de Madrid
  INTERMEDIAE-Matadero
  Paseo de la Chopera, 14
  Tfno. +34 915177287
  arual@medialab-prado.es
  www.medialab-prado.es

  Durante las obras que tienen lugar en MEDIALAB-PRADO (Plaza de las Letras. Alameda,
  15. 28014 Madrid) el personal y la actividad se trasladan temporalmente a Paseo de la
  Chopera, 14. 28045 Madrid (Intermediae-Matadero-Madrid).

  Hello again,

  I add to the information a sent previously some ideas that one of our
  partners, Manufatura Independiente, is working on:
  http://blogs.lgru.net/ft/theme/abstracting-craft/tools-for-a-read-write-world-2


  It's a kind of visual toolkit that could be used as an ingredient for
  the generative version/poster.

  Please it would be great if you could give us an answer before Monday.
  Sorry for the hurry but as you see times are really tight...

  Thank you,

  Laura

  hi laura,

  sorry for the delay. we are quite busy lately and therefore had some
  discussion how and what it could be to work with you for the lgm.

  in general we feel really honoroued by your request and beside some
  general questions, to which i'll refer later, we discussed following
  major approaches (very rough, just to let you know):

  - generative dingbats fonts (generated in x versions). The fonts will be
  available free/libre. as an online generator a simple interface could be
  used to enter text (that then will be images ) to 'create' poster
  versions. what we like about the idea is, that to use a font is pretty
  straight forward, since a font is something like the most common
  denominator for people designing with computers, from amateur to expert.
  to create stuff you do not even need to use dtp software, but can start
  simply with a word processor.

  - generative illustrations of interconnected things/actions (similar to
  the stuff i did for the linux audio conference
  (http://www.lafkon.net/what/is/lac2008) and which has evolved during the
  years. to give you an idea, you can see the latest, very downstripped
  examples here:

  http://www.forkable.eu/generators/merelles/o/free/_schmiede12/Schmiede-121309120831.gif
  http://www.forkable.eu/generators/merelles/o/free/_schmiede12/Schmiede-121209205352.gif
  http://www.forkable.eu/generators/merelles/o/free/_schmiede12/Schmiede-121209191451.gif
  http://www.forkable.eu/generators/merelles/o/free/_schmiede12/Schmiede-121209190409.gif

  just browse the directory to see more. the illustration would in your
  case focus on graphic design. output and source code is shared as
  free/libre/open source software. we could also imagine an online
  interface for this to generate and store versions.

  - we had some other ideas, but these are not yet elaborated enough to
  write them down ;)

  and now my questions:

   > "Tools for a read-write world"

  this is the title for the lgm and the workshop weeks and the campaign
  would cover both?

   > Design and programming of an online generative tool to create the
   > graphic materials for the campaign in a way that includes audience's
   > voice (text, images)

  until now we did not come up with a really convincing solution for that.
  for our past floss projects we share output and source code, but
  consciousely denied to provide an easy/out-of-the-box design solution
  for public audiences, because we did not find a satisfying balance
  between usability and boredom. do YOU have more precise ideas about this?

   > Production will happen in Madrid

  just to note: past poster projects were produced using b/w laser
  printers (for makeart 2010 a combination of laser/offset) because we did
  not have a single poster but a lot variations, since the focus was on
  the generative process and outcome. this has been from experience a bit
  more complicated and cost-intensive than a classical offset print.

  we'll try to get together something visual on the weekend and keep you
  posted.

  best regards,
  christoph

  On 11/23/2012 05:52 PM, Christoph Haag wrote:
  > hi laura,
  >
  > sorry for the delay. we are quite busy lately and therefore had some
  > discussion how and what it could be to work with you for the lgm.
  >
  > in general we feel really honoroued by your request and beside some
  > general questions, to which i'll refer later, we discussed following
  > major approaches (very rough, just to let you know):
  >
  > - generative dingbats fonts (generated in x versions). The fonts will
  > be available free/libre. as an online generator a simple interface
  > could be used to enter text (that then will be images ) to 'create'
  > poster versions. what we like about the idea is, that to use a font is
  > pretty straight forward, since a font is something like the most
  > common denominator for people designing with computers, from amateur
  > to expert. to create stuff you do not even need to use dtp software,
  > but can start simply with a word processor.
  >
  > - generative illustrations of interconnected things/actions (similar
  > to the stuff i did for the linux audio conference
  > (http://www.lafkon.net/what/is/lac2008) and which has evolved during
  > the years. to give you an idea, you can see the latest, very
  > downstripped examples here:
  >
  > http://www.forkable.eu/generators/merelles/o/free/_schmiede12/Schmiede-121309120831.gif
  >
  > http://www.forkable.eu/generators/merelles/o/free/_schmiede12/Schmiede-121209205352.gif
  >
  > http://www.forkable.eu/generators/merelles/o/free/_schmiede12/Schmiede-121209191451.gif
  >
  > http://www.forkable.eu/generators/merelles/o/free/_schmiede12/Schmiede-121209190409.gif
  >
  >
  > just browse the directory to see more. the illustration would in your
  > case focus on graphic design. output and source code is shared as
  > free/libre/open source software. we could also imagine an online
  > interface for this to generate and store versions.
  >
  > - we had some other ideas, but these are not yet elaborated enough to
  > write them down ;)
  >
  > and now my questions:
  >
  >> "Tools for a read-write world"
  >
  > this is the title for the lgm and the workshop weeks and the campaign
  > would cover both?
  >
  >> Design and programming of an online generative tool to create the
  >> graphic materials for the campaign in a way that includes audience's
  >> voice (text, images)
  >
  > until now we did not come up with a really convincing solution for
  > that. for our past floss projects we share output and source code, but
  > consciousely denied to provide an easy/out-of-the-box design solution
  > for public audiences, because we did not find a satisfying balance
  > between usability and boredom. do YOU have more precise ideas about this?
  >
  >> Production will happen in Madrid
  >
  > just to note: past poster projects were produced using b/w laser
  > printers (for makeart 2010 a combination of laser/offset) because we
  > did not have a single poster but a lot variations, since the focus was
  > on the generative process and outcome. this has been from experience a
  > bit more complicated and cost-intensive than a classical offset print.
  >
  > we'll try to get together something visual on the weekend and keep you
  > posted.

  Hello Christoph,

  Thank you again for your enthusiasm, we are really happy!
  I send a few comments on our side and try to answer your questions

  On 11/23/2012 05:52 PM, Christoph Haag wrote:
  > - generative dingbats fonts (generated in x versions). The fonts will
  > be available free/libre. as an online generator a simple interface
  > could be used to enter text (that then will be images ) to 'create'
  > poster versions. what we like about the idea is, that to use a font is
  > pretty straight forward, since a font is something like the most

  > the years. to give you an idea, you can see the latest, very
  > downstripped examples here:
  >
  > http://www.forkable.eu/generators/merelles/o/free/_schmiede12/Schmiede-121309120831.gif
  >
  > http://www.forkable.eu/generators/merelles/o/free/_schmiede12/Schmiede-121209205352.gif
  >
  > http://www.forkable.eu/generators/merelles/o/free/_schmiede12/Schmiede-121209191451.gif
  >
  > http://www.forkable.eu/generators/merelles/o/free/_schmiede12/Schmiede-121209190409.gif
  >

  > just browse the directory to see more. the illustration would in your
  > case focus on graphic design. output and source code is shared as
  > free/libre/open source software. we could also imagine an online
  > interface for this to generate and store versions.
  >
  > - we had some other ideas, but these are not yet elaborated enough to
  > write them down ;)

  That all looks great, and it makes a lot of sense that the campaign
  continues existing work for related events. Some questions:
  - Here you have different images, but they are all "similar" in a way.
  How would this work with more diverse images? Do you think then adding
  new images would be possible?
  - Could we think about how different 'slogans' could function,
  'interfere' with, talk back to the images? Or do you think this would be
  too complicated?
  - What do you think about using color?

  > and now my questions:
  >
  >> "Tools for a read-write world"
  >
  > this is the title for the lgm and the workshop weeks and the campaign
  > would cover both?

  The general title would be "Future Tools" (that makes it shorter and
  easier I guess), and that would cover lgm and workshop  (so we don't
  need to use the title "Tools for a read-write world", which refers only
  to the workshop)

  >> Design and programming of an online generative tool to create the
  >> graphic materials for the campaign in a way that includes audience's
  >> voice (text, images)
  >
  > until now we did not come up with a really convincing solution for
  > that. for our past floss projects we share output and source code, but
  > consciousely denied to provide an easy/out-of-the-box design solution
  > for public audiences, because we did not find a satisfying balance
  > between usability and boredom. do YOU have more precise ideas about this?

  I understand. Here more explanation on our side was needed of course :).
  It is not our intention to provide an immediate and, as you say,
  easy/out-of-the-box way in which anyone can transform their ideas in
  posters. We were planning to use different specific means to prepare and
  facilitate this inclusion of different voices in the campaign. For
  example, we are working with local design schools and have the
  complicity of some teachers to generate this kind of process with
  students; we have contact with the professional graphic designers
  association in Madrid and could make some interviews with members; we
  have a community of Medialab-Prado's regular local users, which are very
  active and can get involve through mailing list or meetings; we plan to
  develop some activities in the neighbourhood around MLP to spread the
  word and get neighbors and local business involved; etc. And of course
  we can expect the involvement of the libre graphics community and all
  the international network around this project (Constant, Worm, Piksel
  and other organizations are in it) The idea is to collect different
  slogans in the form of questions which reflect the different ideas and
  also prejudices that diverse groups have around libre graphics, free
  software, or free culture. That would be our job. Then I imagine we
  could have a repository of those slogans, maybe images too?, that anyone
  could use to generate new images online...
  Does this make sense for you?

  >> Production will happen in Madrid
  >
  > just to note: past poster projects were produced using b/w laser
  > printers (for makeart 2010 a combination of laser/offset) because we
  > did not have a single poster but a lot variations, since the focus was
  > on the generative process and outcome. this has been from experience a
  > bit more complicated and cost-intensive than a classical offset print.

  Yes. The idea is to have at the end just one "official" poster. The rest
  of the production (other posters, but we think that other derived
  outcomes could be stickers, pins, flyers, clothes...) would be
  "home-made" at Medialab.

  Let's keep on talking, sure there are many other things...

  Best regards,

  Laura

  hi laura,

  thanks for your answers so far.

  > I understand. Here more explanation on our side was needed of course :).
  > It is not our intention to provide an immediate and, as you say,
  > easy/out-of-the-box way in which anyone can transform their ideas in
  > posters. We were planning to use different specific means to prepare and
  > facilitate this inclusion of different voices in the campaign. For
  > example, we are working with local design schools and have the
  > complicity of some teachers to generate this kind of process with
  > students; we have contact with the professional graphic designers
  > association in Madrid and could make some interviews with members; we
  > have a community of Medialab-Prado's regular local users, which are very
  > active and can get involve through mailing list or meetings; we plan to
  > develop some activities in the neighbourhood around MLP to spread the
  > word and get neighbors and local business involved; etc. And of course
  > we can expect the involvement of the libre graphics community and all
  > the international network around this project (Constant, Worm, Piksel
  > and other organizations are in it) The idea is to collect different
  > slogans in the form of questions which reflect the different ideas and
  > also prejudices that diverse groups have around libre graphics, free
  > software, or free culture. That would be our job. Then I imagine we
  > could have a repository of those slogans, maybe images too?, that anyone
  > could use to generate new images online...
  > Does this make sense for you?

  to make sure i got the idea: the input would/should be on a 'content'
  level like slogans (or images) of people's view on the floss graphics
  world. and WE would use this input for the design for lgm?

  or are you imagining something (=software) that is easy enough (from the
  technical perspective) that it could be used in workshops, e.g. for
  design students?

  i'll keep you posted with some more visual stuff soon.

  best regards,
  christoph

  On 12/02/2012 11:45 PM, Christoph Haag wrote:
  Hi Christoph again,

  sorry for the delay in answering

  > to make sure i got the idea: the input would/should be on a 'content'
  > level like slogans (or images) of people's view on the floss graphics
  > world. and WE would use this input for the design for lgm?
  >
  > or are you imagining something (=software) that is easy enough (from
  > the technical perspective) that it could be used in workshops, e.g.
  > for design students?

  Yes, input would be on the "content" level. What we would need a
  tool/interface  that would generate a diversity of results which have
  something like a "signature" (Future Tools, dates...) and then a
  composition using slogans and images provided by people through this
  "mediated" process of workshops, interviews, etc. Something like the
  examples of UNIZO.be and lust.nl you can see at the hotglue site. This
  online tool/interface should then allow user manipulation to compose the
  results, but it doesn't mean you need to develop an easy-to-use software
  Of course the software itself should still be open source, but this is
  not in the first place where design students and other collectives are
  invited in.

  I hope that makes it a more clear...
  >
  > i'll keep you posted with some more visual stuff soon.

  Great.
  It might be would to have a phone conversation in the following days,
  Can i call you on Friday in the morning? I have this number fron your
  site:  0821 8852255

  best!

  laura

  hi laura and all,

  i put a technical/visual mockup online at
  http://www.lafkon.net/exchange/lgm2013/121214/ . it provides an
  interface were people add text to generative illustrations/situtations
  and create something like microstories, which will be stored and added
  directly to the pool of situations. this way we would collect voices
  from the public in a very simple way, which will also allow people to
  interact in asynchronous way (e.g. people who are sceptical about floss
  can add a question and somebody who is browsing the site later and
  stumbles upon this question can answer it). in the end these
  microstories will be used to populate a bigger scenario, which will
  provide the main visual element for the poster campaign. the variations
  will be much bigger (it's just a test right now) for the final version,
  but i think one gets the idea. the text right now is mostly blindtext,
  sometimes funny, sometimes not. if you have questions we can also have a
  phone call tomorrow.

  best regards,
  christoph

  hey Christoph,

  I send some comments based on suggestions sent by Hajo, mixed with my
  added thoughts, I hope it makes sense ;):

  - We would like to avoid looking too nerd. In the use of the online
  interface we can expect and we want to include all kinds of questions,
  from the most nerdy to the most uninitiated ones, from the ones coming
  from the libre graphics or floss world to the ones coming from this
  "outside" world that we would like to reach. This is very nice because
  it can be diverse and complex, but we should somehow make sure that the
  final posters or images don't look too "nerdy" or too technical.
  -Questions, and answers?. Depending on the contexts, giving answers
  could give the impression of being dogmatic and could exclude people.
  /Hajo: "To my idea people should answer the questions themselves when
  they see the posters. I would suggest to stick with questions and let
  the event self be the answer/". And I was thinking: on the one hand I
  like very much the idea of people giving their personal answer to
  questions posted by others, in an asynchronous way. That can happen in
  the online site. But for the final images we use it might be better to
  not give answers, because then it would be general and not personal
  answers...I guess we can combine both possibilities. What do you think?

  I think you were out these days, at least 27th that I remember. If you
  are back on Friday I can call you. I will be on Holidays next week, but
  tell me and I will try to call you when you are back.

  I wish you all a happy 2013!

  laura

  hi laura,

  thanks for the update.

  > I send some comments based on suggestions sent by Hajo, mixed with my
  > added thoughts, I hope it makes sense ;):
  >
  > We would like to avoid looking too nerd. In the use of the online
  > interface we can expect and we want to include all kinds of questions,
  > from the most nerdy to the most uninitiated ones, from the ones coming
  > from the libre graphics or floss world to the ones coming from this
  > "outside" world that we would like to reach. This is very nice because
  > it can be diverse and complex, but we should somehow make sure that the
  > final posters or images don't look too "nerdy" or too technical.
  > -Questions, and answers?. Depending on the contexts, giving answers
  > could give the impression of being dogmatic and could exclude people.
  > /Hajo: "To my idea people should answer the questions themselves when
  > they see the posters. I would suggest to stick with questions and let
  > the event self be the answer/". And I was thinking: on the one hand I
  > like very much the idea of people giving their personal answer to
  > questions posted by others, in an asynchronous way. That can happen in
  > the online site. But for the final images we use it might be better to
  > not give answers, because then it would be general and not personal
  > answers...I guess we can combine both possibilities. What do you think?

  i think that's fine.

  > I think you were out these days, at least 27th that I remember. If you
  > are back on Friday I can call you. I will be on Holidays next week, but
  > tell me and I will try to call you when you are back.

  i will be in the studio from monday on, so we best have a conversation
  after your holidays. meanwhile i keep you posted.

  > I wish you all a happy 2013!

  same for all of you!

  best regards,
  christoph

  >>>> floss can add a question and somebody who is browsing the site later

  hi laura and all,

  here is preview of our design for lgm, based on the ongoing conversation.

  http://www.lafkon.net/exchange/lgm2013/130108/

  to continue and complement the existing lgm design we picked up the 15°
  angle of the logo and the osp din. for the 'voices from the public' we
  use a rendering of the serreria font with in/outlets, to which different
  'sorts of actions' and speechbubbles (q&a) are connected. this design
  can be adapted for different kind of uses (website,input
  interface,etcpp.). let me hear what you think, so we can coordinate the
  next steps.

  best regards,
  christoph

  Dear Christoph,

  Thanks a lot!

  We had some exchange about the proposal, I send some comments and
  questions to continue.

  - We like a lot like the 'style' of the posters; very nice mashups of
  many things, which go from abstract/aesthetic to sloganist. It also will
  work well to use these typographic patterns on the LGM website. As we
  said slogans can change from context to context, but for the street very
  clear slogans like "do i really need photoshop to be a graphic
  designer?" would work perfectly.

  - We have the feeling that a bit bit more clear reading of the slogans
  would help, and maybe also a bit more organic, "soft" look? ;)

  - Just to consider, we are not sure, the possibility of using colors?

  Questions:

  - How do you see the online interface at this point? I liked a lot the
  idea of seeing _people_ talking to each other in the proposal you sent.
  Once we have the interface online, we can start our work to invite
  people to use it in different ways and contexts. When do you think this
  can happen?

  - At this point, how do you see the printing process, do you have an
  idea of what special needs would we have?

  And last thing: as soon as possible we would need a a sticker / banner
  to print and spread. Our deadline for that is 5 feb, when FOSDEM in
  Brussels starts.

  Let's continue dialogue (I think Hajo might want to add some things
  too), and we can have a phone conversation at the beginning of next week.

  Best Regards!

  Laura

  hi laura and all,

  > - We like a lot like the 'style' of the posters; very nice mashups of
  > many things, which go from abstract/aesthetic to sloganist. It also will
  > work well to use these typographic patterns on the LGM website. As we
  > said slogans can change from context to context, but for the street very
  > clear slogans like "do i really need photoshop to be a graphic
  > designer?" would work perfectly.

  thanks. i suggest we'll collect all posters online and do some sorting
  before the actual printing. i am curious what slogans will come in.

  > - We have the feeling that a bit bit more clear reading of the slogans
  > would help, and maybe also a bit more organic, "soft" look? ;)

  from my point, i think current style strikes a good balance between
  complexity and readability. still complex enough to make it interesting
  to look and analyse, still readable.

  i am not sure what you mean by organic/soft.

  > - Just to consider, we are not sure, the possibility of using colors?

  we decided to use one lead color for the logo and some key elements
  only, while the main appearance sticks to plain black/white. This is
  owed to some extent to the reproduction prerequisites for the generative
  graphic part of the identity, but we also regard the reduction in color
  aesthetic feature.

  http://www.lafkon.net/exchange/lgm2013/130113

  > - How do you see the online interface at this point? I liked a lot the
  > idea of seeing _people_ talking to each other in the proposal you sent.
  > Once we have the interface online, we can start our work to invite
  > people to use it in different ways and contexts. When do you think this
  > can happen?

  by now the interface is technically working, but we did not really start
  to work on the design. i suggest we fixate some general basics first
  (e.g. logo design) and keep your suggestions for the interface in mind.

  > - At this point, how do you see the printing process, do you have an
  > idea of what special needs would we have?

  the posters for lgm 2013 consist of a generative part, which is made
  from the audiences input, and an static layer. the static color layer is
  produced in an offset print run on which the generative layer will be
  added with b/w laser printer. we planned to do a2 posters, therefore we
  would need to find a printshop for the offset and for the b/w laser
  part, which is not that common in a2 (compared to a3). it could be one
  or two different printers. biggest problem is according to experience
  the b/w laser part, because you have to find somebody, who does prints
  in a2 and is willing to print on preprinted paper.

  > And last thing: as soon as possible we would need a a sticker / banner
  > to print and spread. Our deadline for that is 5 feb, when FOSDEM in
  > Brussels starts.

  we suggest a sticker version of the lgm 2013 logo.
  http://www.lafkon.net/exchange/lgm2013/130113/

  for this idea we'd need to decide fast and get the data ready before
  17.1. because they do only print at certain dates, but have therefore
  quite cheap offers.

  > Let's continue dialogue (I think Hajo might want to add some things
  > too), and we can have a phone conversation at the beginning of next week.

  you can just call. we're in the studio all week.

  best regards,
  christoph

  STICKERS/FLYERS:

  - Text 'Future Tools' needs to be on the front-side of sticker (OK if it
  repeats on back-side)

  - Text for backside:

  ////////////////

  http://www.libregraphicsmeeting.org

  Future Tools
  Madrid 10-13 April
  Medialab Prado /

  /This spring, the yearly 'Libre Graphics Meeting' and the creative
  prototyping workshop 'Interactivos?’13: Tools for a read-write world'
  join forces to exchange, discuss, produce and imagine Free, Libre and
  Open source tools for graphics and design. The event is a unique
  opportunity for software developers, artists and designers from all over
  the world to get together and collaborate on current and future tools.

  /SPANISH VERSION: //El encuentro anual 'Libre Graphics Meeting' y el
  taller de prototipado colaborativo 'Interactivos?’13: Herramientas para
  un mundo legible y editable' unen fuerzas para intercambiar, debatir,
  producir e imaginar herramientas libres y de código abierto para el
  diseño. Este evento es una oportunidad única para desarrolladores de
  software, artistas y diseñadores que quieran colaborar en torno a las
  herramientas del presente y del futuro. /

  -We need to include Madrid-MLP and EU logo at backside too

  POSTERS:

  Include http://www.libregraphicsmeeting.org and http://medialab-prado.es

  Future Tools

  time yes

  Otherwise link for website is enough.

  >   translations?
  >   Which/How many languages?

  stickers/flyers: We need to have 2 versions: Spanish/English paragraph
  at the backside.
  posters: only slogans coming from audience's input need to be
  Spanish/English. The fixed info is only English

  Christoph Haag escribió:
  > hi laura and all,
  >
  >> - We like a lot like the 'style' of the posters; very nice mashups of
  >> many things, which go from abstract/aesthetic to sloganist. It also will
  >> work well to use these typographic patterns on the LGM website. As we
  >> said slogans can change from context to context, but for the street very
  >> clear slogans like "do i really need photoshop to be a graphic
  >> designer?" would work perfectly.
  >
  > thanks. i suggest we'll collect all posters online and do some sorting
  > before the actual printing. i am curious what slogans will come in.
  >
  >> - We have the feeling that a bit bit more clear reading of the slogans
  >> would help, and maybe also a bit more organic, "soft" look? ;)
  >
  > from my point, i think current style strikes a good balance between
  > complexity and readability. still complex enough to make it
  > interesting to look and analyse, still readable.
  >
  > i am not sure what you mean by organic/soft.
  >
  >> - Just to consider, we are not sure, the possibility of using colors?
  >
  > we decided to use one lead color for the logo and some key elements
  > only, while the main appearance sticks to plain black/white. This is
  > owed to some extent to the reproduction prerequisites for the
  > generative graphic part of the identity, but we also regard the
  > reduction in color aesthetic feature.
  >
  > http://www.lafkon.net/exchange/lgm2013/130113
  >
  >> - How do you see the online interface at this point? I liked a lot the
  >> idea of seeing _people_ talking to each other in the proposal you sent.
  >> Once we have the interface online, we can start our work to invite
  >> people to use it in different ways and contexts. When do you think this
  >> can happen?
  >
  > by now the interface is technically working, but we did not really
  > start to work on the design. i suggest we fixate some general basics
  > first (e.g. logo design) and keep your suggestions for the interface
  > in mind.
  >
  >> - At this point, how do you see the printing process, do you have an
  >> idea of what special needs would we have?
  >
  > the posters for lgm 2013 consist of a generative part, which is made
  > from the audiences input, and an static layer. the static color layer
  > is produced in an offset print run on which the generative layer will
  > be added with b/w laser printer. we planned to do a2 posters,
  > therefore we would need to find a printshop for the offset and for the
  > b/w laser part, which is not that common in a2 (compared to a3). it
  > could be one or two different printers. biggest problem is according
  > to experience the b/w laser part, because you have to find somebody,
  > who does prints in a2 and is willing to print on preprinted paper.
  >
  >> And last thing: as soon as possible we would need a a sticker / banner
  >> to print and spread. Our deadline for that is 5 feb, when FOSDEM in
  >> Brussels starts.
  >
  > we suggest a sticker version of the lgm 2013 logo.
  > http://www.lafkon.net/exchange/lgm2013/130113/
  >
  > for this idea we'd need to decide fast and get the data ready before
  > 17.1. because they do only print at certain dates, but have therefore
  > quite cheap offers.
  >
  >> Let's continue dialogue (I think Hajo might want to add some things
  >> too), and we can have a phone conversation at the beginning of next
  >> week.
  >
  > you can just call. we're in the studio all week.
  >
  > best regards,
  > christoph

  we would choose this printer

  Outdoor-Sticker A8 (50,5 x 72mm) 100µ
  DureFix white, 4/1-colour, full colour printing on front, one colour
  gray on back, UV finish
  self-adhesive, back slit
  Product: 224

  price for 1000 stickers: 72,14 EUR
  price for 2000 stickers: 99,92 EUR

  since we have english and spanish, we will have the amount two times.

  this way we can have a standard print (square) and save some money.
  if you have a local printer, you would like to work with, that's fine
  for us. you would just need to figure out and then we will send the

  Hello Christoph and Benjamin,

  Last minute we got a chance to put an advertisement in the upcoming issue of Libre
  Graphics Magazine and for this we need your help.

  I understand the 'tool' is not ready yet, but is it possible to send us either a pdf
  like the ones here: http://www.lafkon.net/exchange/lgm2013/130108/

  ... with four changes:

  - Phrase in the background: "So why did Eye-magazine not run an article on it if this
  is so important for designers?"
  - Website address: http://libregraphicsmeeting.org
  - A small credit for you (Lafkon) somewhere!
  - No Google logo

  If you don't have time to adjust the file beyond generating the slogan for us, we
  completely understand -- but I'll still would much appreciate if you could send me an
  svg-file of the slogan by early tomorrow, so I can prepare the page for print. If yes,
  these are the requirements:

  a4 with 5mm bleeds -- 215x307
  right page, inner side no bleed
  full colour
  deadline: Friday Jan 18 21:00 CET
  send print-ready pdf to: regnig@adaptstudio.ca

  Thank you!


  Femke

  hello all,

  the current version for lgm design is online, the plain project
  structure as usual (http://www.forkable.eu/generators/r+w/). most
  interesting at the moment is probably the 'public voices' interface
  (http://www.forkable.eu/generators/r+w/Q&A). i entered the questions
  from the etherpad (which i liked a lot and make me look forward to the
  answers). for the interface i suggest a not-so-public test run during
  the next days, on one hand to get the syncing with poster generator
  right, on the other hand from a usability point of view. feedback welcome.

  missing right now is some kind of documentation, which i will work on
  soonish. furthermore we need to decide something for the lgm website.


  best regards,
  christoph

  hi femke and others,

  first of all, i did oversee the logo from lgm falls under 'Except where
  otherwise stated, all the content CC-BY-SA Libre Graphics Meeting.'
  therefore we will change the disclaimer appropriately.

  to explain:
  for the repository we try to keep some way of a sense-making
  differentiation for different copyrights of different files. this
  disclaimer is like the standard disclaimer for files that contain things
  we've not created ourselves (like the lgm logo) or we are not sure
  wether to put in under the standard triple licensing
  (gpl,gfdl,cc-by-sa). for the press folder it's not so obvious, a better
  example might be the sticker files
  (http://www.forkable.eu/generators/r+w/o/free/sla/) which contain logos
  for the eu programme and medialab prado for which we do not have the
  right to put it under any free license. since we do not want to exclude
  these files from download, we put the disclaimer.

  best regards,
  christoph

  hi christoph & benjamin,

  femke has asked me if it would be possible to host the r+w online
  campaign on the lgm server...

  i don't see any problem with it, except that i don't know what is it
  needed to get it to work.
  and i think that it would be nice to host it on the lgm server.

  i've skimmed through the do.sh file and other files in the repository
  and it looks like it's using gs, latex, inscape, scribus and lot of
  other things.

  sadly, it won't be easy to get all this to work on the server.
  lot of packages should be installed -- and maintained -- for it.


  so, the first question is: what are the conditions to get the r+w
  software to work?


  but, maybe, a better question would be: would it be possible to serve
  from the lgm site the files generated by forkable.eu/generators/r+w/ ?

  i could not see what is inside the Q&A file, so i have no idea how the
  code that is serving the web page looks like.

  so, even if we want to just proxy the site on the lgm site i need to
  know more about how r+w is working.


  basically: shell and basic web technologies are available on the lgm
  server or can be made available.
  desktop related libraries are unlikely to get installed by the admin.


  have a nice day
  a.l.e

  hi ale,

  > femke has asked me if it would be possible to host the r+w online
  > campaign on the lgm server...
  >
  > i don't see any problem with it, except that i don't know what is it
  > needed to get it to work.
  > and i think that it would be nice to host it on the lgm server.

  let's see if we can make it ;)

  > i've skimmed through the do.sh file and other files in the repository
  > and it looks like it's using gs, latex, inscape, scribus and lot of
  > other things.

  > sadly, it won't be easy to get all this to work on the server.
  > lot of packages should be installed -- and maintained -- for it.

  that's basically the same issue we have. what you see on the webspace is
  non-functional mirror of our local production environment. since most
  scripts are experimental and therefore pretty unstable we do not run any
  of them on this server, because there are running some services we don't
  want to miss due to errors.

  > so, the first question is: what are the conditions to get the r+w
  > software to work?

  the software is basically divided in three parts: *first* the online
  interface which is php (with write access to one folder) to collect the
  input from the q&a page. for that more or less a basic webserver
  configuration will do it. that's all for the website.
  the rest runs on a local machine: *second*: a script for synchronizing
  (http://www.forkable.eu/generators/r+w/update.sh), which updates the
  files from http://www.forkable.eu/generators/r+w/o/free/voice/ via wget,
  triggers do.sh (the *third* part) and uploads the generated files via
  ftp with write access to a single folder. update.sh is currently hidden,
  following a 'security through obscurity' approach, since i am not
  completely sure, if i am doing something really dumb ;) i know, not very
  open, but saves me some nerves.

  do.sh provides the rendering of the posters. it's not really intended to
  run on the online machine for the reasons mentioned above. i developed
  on debian 6.0.5 (squeeze) and experienced some problems when i ported it
  to the machine with debian 5.0.10 (lenny), where it's currently running,
  but nothing dramatic. so it should be doable to also transfer this part
  to any local machine.

  > but, maybe, a better question would be: would it be possible to serve
  > from the lgm site the files generated by forkable.eu/generators/r+w/ ?

  to serve from the lgm website we could simply move the online part (php)
  and would need ftp access (depending on the admins state of paranoia
  something different) to upload the generated files. where these files
  get generated depends on available possibilites. could be on our machine
  or i could assist somebody by getting the software running.

  > i could not see what is inside the Q&A file, so i have no idea how the
  > code that is serving the web page looks like.
  > so, even if we want to just proxy the site on the lgm site i need to
  > know more about how r+w is working.

  did i answer all questions? a proxy version would be most probably the
  simplest solution. so let me know what you think.


  best regards,
  christoph

  hi ale,

  i prepared the files, that should be able to be set up on the lgm
  server: http://www.lafkon.net/exchange/lgm2013/130131_r+w_qa.tar.gz

  the file is rather big (203mb) because it contains all posters generated
  until now. in the package are two folders/versions:

  r+w_qa
  ----------------
  contains php and necessary files,
  depending on a suitable apache configuration
  -> mod_rewrite, nothing exotic,
  links to the poster pages go to forkable.eu
  = this is the stripped down version

  r+w_qa_+POSTER
  ----------------
  contains php and necessary files,
  depending on a suitable apache configuration
  -> mod_rewrite, nothing exotic,
  poster/thumbnails/indexes are included and
  can be synchronized via shell script (mirror_poster.sh)
  using wget

  for the automatic generation of the posters i will mirror txt files from
  the o/free/voice directory on the lgm server to our local machine,
  therefore i will need the url und +Indexes for apache must be enabled.

  i hope i didn't forget anything, if there any problems, just write.

  best regards,
  christoph

  hallo christoph,

  > i prepared the files, that should be able to be set up on the lgm
  > server: http://www.lafkon.net/exchange/lgm2013/130131_r+w_qa.tar.gz
  > 
  > the file is rather big (203mb) because it contains all posters
  > generated until now. in the package are two folders/versions:
  > 
  > r+w_qa
  > ----------------
  > contains php and necessary files,
  > depending on a suitable apache configuration
  > ->mod_rewrite, nothing exotic,
  > links to the poster pages go to forkable.eu
  > =3D this is the stripped down version
  > 
  > r+w_qa_+POSTER
  > ----------------
  > contains php and necessary files,
  > depending on a suitable apache configuration
  > ->mod_rewrite, nothing exotic,
  > poster/thumbnails/indexes are included and
  > can be synchronized via shell script (mirror_poster.sh)
  > using wget
  >

  > from the o/free/voice directory on the lgm server to our local
  > machine, therefore i will need the url und +Indexes for apache must
  > be enabled.

  > i hope i didn't forget anything, if there any problems, just write.

  i had a look at the two php file i could find

  make_interface.php
  post.php

  the first one shows the interface and the form. i didn't understand
  some details but -- basically -- looks ok to me.

  on the other side, post.php starts with a redirection and is never
  executed.

  on the lgm server at

  http://libregraphicsmeeting.org/2013/r+w_qa/

  i've put the following files from the stripped down version

  make_interface.php
  post.php
  q+a.css

  sadly, the people in charge of the server refuse to activate
  the support for the .htaccess files. so we will have to rely on a
  rewrite that is hardcoded by them in the apache config files or avoid
  it.
  i'm going for the "avoid it" option for now.

  so... i've renamed make_interface.php to o/free/voiceindex.php ... and
  made the links work also without .htaccess (diff is attached).

  i've also renamed o/free/voice/ALLVOICES.php to o/free/voice/index.php
  and point the link to o/free/voice/ (and so remove the ALL) and patched
  the url to the individual q&a.


  voilÃ , now comes the write part.

  i haven't touched at the post script. it's trivial to get it to add new
  files to the o/ directory, but it's still not clear to me how do you
  want to share them with your computer and generate the up to date PDFs.

  once that part is solved, i think that we can go live with the r+w_qa
  on the lgm server...


  voilÃ , i'm waiting for some explaination on the write part :-)
  if you want we can setup an irc rendez-vous... i should be able to be
  online tomorrow (friday) afternoon or on saturday the whole day.

  (sadly, i guess that all i can offer on the server is to send a
  notification when a new question or answer is added and allow you to
  get the new files by http... but it may already be enough... who knows?)


  i wish you a wonderful evening
  a.l.e

  hallo ale,

  On 07/02/13 16:49, ale rimoldi wrote:
  > hallo christoph,
  > i had a look at the two php file i could find
  >
  > make_interface.php
  > post.php
  >
  > the first one shows the interface and the form. i didn't understand
  > some details but -- basically -- looks ok to me.
  >
  > on the other side, post.php starts with a redirection and is never
  > executed.
  >
  > on the lgm server at
  >
  > http://libregraphicsmeeting.org/2013/r+w_qa/
  >
  > i've put the following files from the stripped down version
  >
  > make_interface.php
  > post.php
  > q+a.css

  super. the main difference is basically that the 'see posters for this
  conversation' is always there (not checked back if posters exist) and we
  us external links, but it's much easier this way and we avoid a lot of
  hassle for the syncing. so i think it's great this way.

  > sadly, the people in charge of the server refuse to activate
  > the support for the .htaccess files. so we will have to rely on a
  > rewrite that is hardcoded by them in the apache config files or avoid
  > it.
  > i'm going for the "avoid it" option for now.
  >
  > so... i've renamed make_interface.php to o/free/voiceindex.php ... and
  > made the links work also without .htaccess (diff is attached).
  >
  > i've also renamed o/free/voice/ALLVOICES.php to o/free/voice/index.php
  > and point the link to o/free/voice/ (and so remove the ALL) and patched
  > the url to the individual q&a.

  also great. the only thing i would suggest is to change the folder name
  from 'r+w_qa' to simple 'r+w'


  > voilà, now comes the write part.
  >
  > i haven't touched at the post script. it's trivial to get it to add new
  > files to the o/ directory, but it's still not clear to me how do you
  > want to share them with your computer and generate the up to date PDFs.

  i just download/mirror the text files to the local machine with wget
  (only downloading files with a newer timestamp on the server). i assume
  it will not be possible to get a directory listing, but i attached a php
  file that will do the job.

  > (sadly, i guess that all i can offer on the server is to send a
  > notification when a new question or answer is added and allow you to
  > get the new files by http... but it may already be enough... who knows?)

  i would do this by cron about every 30 minutes and check the existence
  of new files on the local machine. so if it is no problem that i send an
  automated request about every 30 minutes, this should work.

  i will send you an up to date folder with input from forkable.eu and
  then disable the interface there, before we put the lgm version live

  > i wish you a wonderful evening

  same for you.
  thank you.

  christoph

  input will only happen on the lgm site. i set up a git repository for
  the lgm voices at https://github.com/lafkon/var.lgm.voice so we can do
  basic spelling corrections,etcpp (as femke suggested).

  to go live we would just need to:

  - change the name from r+w_qa to just and r+w
  - place the list.php i sent you

  repository
  - on the bottom of q&a page are two links (*|*) to vector versions of
  the random characters. these links do not work. did you upload the files?

  >> contains php and necessary files,
  >> depending on a suitable apache configuration

  >> can be synchronized via shell script (mirror_poster.sh)

  On 30/01/13 11:01, Laura Fernández wrote:
  > Next week Miryam Cea (in cc) will be back in Madrid from a residency
  > with Constant-OSP, and we will start working also to arrange the
  > printing for the posters. We said deadline for "official" posters is
  > March 15th, I guess having more or less a month to circulate the tool
  > and gather q&a should be enough to start. And then we need to think how
  > are we going to select the slogans...

  hi miryam,

  as i heard you will take care of the poster production so i will start
  with some explanations. the basic principle is that we will combine two
  printing methods to have an color as well a generative part.

  the color (=static) part of the posters will be produced as offset
  prints. because for offset printing a printing plate has to be produced
  it's not suitable for the generative part, since it does not make sense
  to produce a printing plate for a single print (+ it's not affordable).
  therefore we will print a certain amount of color prints, which will be
  overlayed in the next step with the generative part. for the offset
  layer you get the file here:

  http://www.forkable.eu/generators/r+w/i/free/svg/130211_SUBLINE-10_OFFSET-ONLY.pdf

  the generative part will be produced as b/w laser prints put above the
  color layer. these are the files which are automatically generated (and
  will be selected before the final printing process):

  e.g.:
  http://www.forkable.eu/generators/r+w/o/__/LGM-2013_3c8407f6_1360052690.pdf
  http://www.forkable.eu/generators/r+w/o/__/LGM-2013_7096a15c_1360052845.pdf
  http://www.forkable.eu/generators/r+w/o/__/LGM-2013_f52dbd2e_1360053006.pdf
  ...

  the actual challenge is to find a printer who is willing to realise such
  a process, because it's not a standard workflow. since production will
  take place in madrid, it'd be you, who has to find a cooperating printer
  ;) possible scenarios might be:

  1. find a printer who provides offset as well as laser printing.
  2. find two separate printers.

  the main problem is that a lot of printers are not easy to convince to
  insert preprinted paper into their machines. this might be easier for
  scenario 1, since the printer has an overlook over the whole process.

  so far our experiences have been, another problem is to find a printer
  who offers offset AND laser printing above a certain size (>A3) for a
  reasonable price. the best direction for cheap b/w laser prints might be
  somebody who offers printing for architectural plans (which is often
  called cad plotting). but this would probably mean to have the offset
  layer printed somewhere else and then convince the printer to print on
  these sheets.

  i put an example of the prints for make art in the sticker package i
  sent to medialab prado. perhaps it useful to show to a printer. what you
  see there and is important is also the quality of the laser print, which
  is really good covering.

  if you have an questions, don't hesitate to ask.

  best regards,
  christoph

  Hi Christoph,

  Yes, I´ll take care of the poster production. I am working to find a
  cooperating printer, who provides offset and laser printing. I´ll try to
  find a sponsor printer, the production is very small but the diffusión
  and repercusión for the printer will be very big. I will be reporting...

  best regards
  Myriam



  El 11/02/13 17:20, Christoph Haag escribió:
  > On 30/01/13 11:01, Laura Fernández wrote:
  >> Next week Miryam Cea (in cc) will be back in Madrid from a residency
  >> with Constant-OSP, and we will start working also to arrange the
  >> printing for the posters. We said deadline for "official" posters is
  >> March 15th, I guess having more or less a month to circulate the tool
  >> and gather q&a should be enough to start. And then we need to think how
  >> are we going to select the slogans...
  >
  > hi miryam,
  >
  > as i heard you will take care of the poster production so i will start
  > with some explanations. the basic principle is that we will combine
  > two printing methods to have an color as well a generative part.
  >
  > the color (=static) part of the posters will be produced as offset
  > prints. because for offset printing a printing plate has to be
  > produced it's not suitable for the generative part, since it does not
  > make sense to produce a printing plate for a single print (+ it's not
  > affordable). therefore we will print a certain amount of color prints,
  > which will be overlayed in the next step with the generative part. for
  > the offset layer you get the file here:
  >
  > http://www.forkable.eu/generators/r+w/i/free/svg/130211_SUBLINE-10_OFFSET-ONLY.pdf
  >
  >
  > the generative part will be produced as b/w laser prints put above the
  > color layer. these are the files which are automatically generated
  > (and will be selected before the final printing process):
  >
  > e.g.:
  > http://www.forkable.eu/generators/r+w/o/__/LGM-2013_3c8407f6_1360052690.pdf
  >
  > http://www.forkable.eu/generators/r+w/o/__/LGM-2013_7096a15c_1360052845.pdf
  >
  > http://www.forkable.eu/generators/r+w/o/__/LGM-2013_f52dbd2e_1360053006.pdf
  >
  > ...
  >
  > the actual challenge is to find a printer who is willing to realise
  > such a process, because it's not a standard workflow. since production
  > will take place in madrid, it'd be you, who has to find a cooperating
  > printer ;) possible scenarios might be:
  >
  > 1. find a printer who provides offset as well as laser printing.
  > 2. find two separate printers.
  >
  > the main problem is that a lot of printers are not easy to convince to
  > insert preprinted paper into their machines. this might be easier for
  > scenario 1, since the printer has an overlook over the whole process.
  >
  > so far our experiences have been, another problem is to find a printer
  > who offers offset AND laser printing above a certain size (>A3) for a
  > reasonable price. the best direction for cheap b/w laser prints might
  > be somebody who offers printing for architectural plans (which is
  > often called cad plotting). but this would probably mean to have the
  > offset layer printed somewhere else and then convince the printer to
  > print on these sheets.
  >
  > i put an example of the prints for make art in the sticker package i
  > sent to medialab prado. perhaps it useful to show to a printer. what
  > you see there and is important is also the quality of the laser print,
  > which is really good covering.
  >
  > if you have an questions, don't hesitate to ask.
  >
  > best regards,
  > christoph

  hallo christoph

  the script is online:

  http://libregraphicsmeeting.org/2013/r+w/o/get/update.php

  you can run it to get the latest 20 changes. you can run it again to
  get the next 20.

  i've just tried to run it without the limit and it could download
  all the 400 files... but it takes several minutes.
  i fear that running this in an automatic way, could produce
  a timeout somewhere.

  but i can easily remove the limit if it's more of a hassle than it
  helps.


  now, you can now try to change the files on github and see if you can
  get them to update on the lgm server :-)


  if possible, you should put a hook in your push/commit
  script that automatically calls the update.php script.

  we are allowed to run the update.php 60 times in the lapse of an hour
  (without having to authenticate with github, which would make
  everything much more complicated...): it should be more than enough if
  your script pokes the lgm server every 5 minutes for changes.


  if we go the way of the automatic triggering of update.php, i can
  add a GET parameter that makes update.php return a json string
  with the number of changes it has seen and the number of updates it has
  done (or any other way that you can process in the calling script).


  if you wonder how it is done, you can have a peak at the script on
  github:

  https://github.com/aoloe/htdocs-get-github


  have a nice day && happy testing
  a.l.e

  hi alexandre,

  thank you for the web sticker version. it's great!
  i noticed a small problem for the copy/paste code on the lgm website:

  <iframe src=”http://stdin.fr/r+w_qa/” style=”width: 250px; height:
  250px; border: 0; overflow: hidden;”></iframe>

  to include the iframe in a wordpress post i had to change ” -> " to get
  it working. you're using right double quotation mark as html entities
  (&#8221;), when it actually should be plain quotation marks.

  <iframe src="http://stdin.fr/r+w_qa/" style="width: 250px; height:
  250px; border: 0; overflow: hidden;"></iframe>

  best regards,
  christoph

  >> Dear Christoph,

  >> We're very pleased to welcome you in Variable next week for the

  >> at this stage.
  >>
  >> The programme we propose is divided in three parts. Thursday morning,
  >> we'll start at 10h with introductions and presentations of various
  >> related projects by participants. Thursday afternoon and Friday
  >> morning, we'll play different "exercices" and practice situations of
  >> collision. Friday afternoon, after lunch, we'll go out for a brief
  >> fieldtrip and, back to Variable, we'll start prototyping following 3
  >> different axes. If sadly you could not follow the full 3 days, maybe
  >> could you schedule your presence according to this slicing and let us
  >> know?

  >> Thursday 21 February
  >> 10:00 – Presentations
  >> Femke Snelting : LGRU, two years after http://lgru.net
  >> Pierre Huyghebaert : Introduction Collision and the Co-position research
  >> Eric Schrijver and John Haltiwanger : Visual Culture
  >> http://git.constantvzw.org/?p=osp.tools.visualculture.git
  >> Alex Leray and Stéphanie Vilayphiou : Brainch and other projects
  >> http://stdin.fr/Works/Brainch
  >> Dave Young : Yet another collaboritive writing tool
  >> http://hendersonsix.com, http://dvyng.com
  >> Christoph Haag (LAFKON) http://www.lafkon.net/
  >> Eleanor Greenhalgh http://ox4.org/~nor/
  >> + other presentations of various related projects by participants.
  >> 12:30 – Lunch
  >> 14:00 – Exercises
  >> Plotter play – territories (Gijs de Heij)
  >> Yet another collaborative editor (Dave Young)
  >> http://www.forkable.eu (Christoph Haag)
  >>
  >> Friday 22 February
  >> 10:00 – Exercise: The People Speak http://www.thepeoplespeak.com
  >> 12:30 – Lunch
  >> 14:00 – Fieldtrip: Border stone meets elephant
  >> Pierre and Femke introduce three possible approaches in response to a
  >> specific cartographic collision. We'll form three groups, to develop
  >> each a mini-prototype.
  >> As a startingpoint, we invite each group to think with us about (one
  >> of) the following questions:
  >> - Could we imagine how reverse placement could bring another approach
  >> to toponomy?
  >> - What if the visualisation of geographic data would allow for tension
  >> and conflict to become visible?
  >> - How to imagine thresholds as relational parameters, rather than as
  >> binary borders?
  >> (research/discussion materials will be provided)
  >>
  >> Saturday 23 February
  >> 10:00 – Prototyping continued
  >> 12:30 – Lunch
  >> 14:00 – Prototyping continued
  >> 17:00 – Presentations and discussion

  Dear Christoph,

  After some research and some more thought we made a new plan for the
  printing of the posters, that we wanted to share with you to know what
  you think.

  On one side, we are seeing that we have little time and little budget
  for the offset/laser combination that we agreed. Myriam was trying to
  get some sponsorship from "friend" printers, but is talking time...On
  the other hand, we thought it is a pity that we don't have more than
  5-10 different printer versions, and that it is a pity too that we don't
  print tha LGM program, which is almost ready by now.

  So, based on those reasons, we thought of a solution which is printing
  only digital laser b/w and doing some manual work afterwards to colour
  the logo in green, with markers, or better stencil and spray...:)

  That would mean, for the file to send to printer, having the logo in
  white and thinking of other way of differentiating the "Future Tools"
  slogan which is not colour.

  We are thinking in printing A3 posters with LGM program in the backside
  (a bit like makeart poster-program you made). If it is digital laser
  printing then we can have as many versions of the poster as we would
  like, because we will merge it all in one single file for the printer.

  In addition to that, we are planning to print at home some A1 posters
  with selected slogans to place in the space of the meeting.

  Please let me know what you think!

  best

  laura

  hi Christoph!

  On 03/04/2013 06:10 PM, Christoph Haag wrote:
  > hi laura, hi myriam,
  >
  > thanks for your efforts.
  >
  >> On one side, we are seeing that we have little time and little budget
  >> for the offset/laser combination that we agreed. Myriam was trying to
  >> get some sponsorship from "friend" printers, but is talking time...On
  >> the other hand, we thought it is a pity that we don't have more than
  >> 5-10 different printer versions, and that it is a pity too that we don't
  >> print tha LGM program, which is almost ready by now.
  >
  > what do you mean by '5-10 different printer versions'?

  to simplify, our previous plan was to choose 5 to 10 versions with
  different slogans for the laser printing on top of the offset printing.
  what we called the "official" posters...mmmh, now that I think about it
  again, i guess that we could have also made all different...

  >> So, based on those reasons, we thought of a solution which is printing
  >> only digital laser b/w and doing some manual work afterwards to colour
  >> the logo in green, with markers, or better stencil and spray...:)
  >
  > a possibility might be making a stamp, which is way more precise/clean
  > than stencil or handcoloring and then we could think of keeping the
  > slogan also in color. eventually one could lasercut linoleum or such?

  good idea, we will think about this option, yes

  >> That would mean, for the file to send to printer, having the logo in
  >> white and thinking of other way of differentiating the "Future Tools"
  >> slogan which is not colour.
  >
  > we could have the future tools slogan inverted, similar to the back of
  > the stickers.

  yes

  >> We are thinking in printing A3 posters with LGM program in the backside
  >> (a bit like makeart poster-program you made). If it is digital laser
  >> printing then we can have as many versions of the poster as we would
  >> like, because we will merge it all in one single file for the printer.
  >
  > good idea. this would be b/w only?

  yes

  >> In addition to that, we are planning to print at home some A1 posters
  >> with selected slogans to place in the space of the meeting.
  >
  > nice. this would be inkjet/color?

  yes.

  We will keep you posted!

  best

  laura

  Dear all,

  You are receiving this message because you indicated that you wanted to help out before
  and/or during LGM.

  We apologize for such a direct call for support, but LGM2013 needs your help in raising
  3500 dollars worth of community funding within the coming three weeks. With a total
  of at least 5000 dollar plus the corporate sponsorship already secured, we will be
  able to reimburse travelcosts for all participants that need it.

  Please post this call, feature the pledgie banner on your website or ... donate.
  Your support makes a difference!

  http://pledgie.com/campaigns/19064

  If you want to discuss ideas for this campaign, you can find us on
  #LGM at irc.freenode.net or subscribe to the organisers mailinglist:
  http://lists.freedesktop.org/mailman/listinfo/libre-graphics-meeting

  Thank you :-)


  Femke

  at the moment i am working on something for the medialab facade.

  since the resolution is quite low, it seems hard to get graphics in a
  satisfying quality, especially for the logo. therefore i am thinking
  about the possibilty to put the logo on the wall as a combination of a
  real object and the display. this means we would cut the logo box out of
  black cardboard, stick it on the wall (as a black silhouette) and have
  it backlit with green color from the display. is this thinkable?
  i am arriving in madrid on the afternoon of 8.april, so from there on i
  could help to take care of this. what do you think?

  Hi Christoph,

  We are going to print some large-format posters large format, with our
  own plotter before the Meeting. We will use the posters in the
  programmes too.

  Finally I found a very good sponsor, it is one of the best printers in
  Madrid. They are going to do the programmes as follows:

  - 500 units
  - Digital print (In colour - we will have green again!)
  - Size (max) 32 x 47cm. (a bit bigger than A3)
  - In one side: a different poster for every copy
  - In the other: the program information (250 English/250 Spanish)
  - And folded twice: horizontally and vertically.

  This is all the information for now. I visited the design schools last
  week,to announce Libre Graphics Meeting. we are hoping for increased
  participation in order to create the generative posters- ;-)

  best
  Myriam

  hi myriam,

  great news!

  i adjusted the script to the new size. now we have a pdf 32x47 cm
  (inclusive 1.5cm bleed at the bottom) -> we will have 32x45.5 cm. the
  pdfs are not 100% pdf-x conform, because the generated layers are output
  from processing and therefore not cmyk. since we have different blacks
  (rich black for the logo and textinfo, plain black for the sponsor logos
  and some kind of rgb black for the graphic), i would suggest we do some
  test prints as soon as possible to see if the result is good.

  http://www.forkable.eu/generators/r+w/o/__/LGM-2013_859a90ff_1363730203.pdf

  http://www.lafkon.net/exchange/lgm2013/130426_r+w_shutdown.tar.gz and
  simply overwrite post.php. the .gz also contains a newer version of the
  serreria font with inverted question/exclamation marks. please do not
  remove the github sync, because i will do some cleaning/correction and
  therefore the files still need to be updated.

  thank you,
  best regards,

  hi femke,

  i'm fine. how are you. there is a git repo with for the questions and
  answers at https://github.com/lafkon/var.lgm.voice which should be
  already spam free, but there are problems syncing with the lgm server
  and i am waiting for ale to do this manually. we closed the input, since
  there was only spam coming in, so what is in the repo would be the final
  state. it's all separate textfiles, the answers (*_A-*.txt) can be
  edited savely (accents are notated as html entities). for the questions
  it's a bit different, because the filename is dependent on the content
  and must change if the content changes. this was more important when the
  interface was still in write mode, you could ignore this for now. so in
  practise it would be the best, if you check out the repository, do the
  edits and send me a pull request. if you have already done the work you
  could send me the stuff as a plain text file and i'll take care of the
  rest. we still will have to have ale do the syncing, just a matter of
  time ;)

  best regards,
  christoph
